      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3> 
      <p>Switzerland contains two terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Western_European_broadleaf_forests" title="Western European broadleaf forests">Western European broadleaf forests</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alps_conifer_and_mixed_forests" title="Alps conifer and mixed forests">Alps conifer and mixed forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-70">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Switzerland's ecosystems can be particularly fragile, because the many delicate valleys separated by high mountains often form unique ecologies. The mountainous regions themselves are also vulnerable, with a rich range of plants not found at other altitudes, and experience some pressure from visitors and grazing. The climatic, geological and topographical conditions of the alpine region make for a very fragile ecosystem that is particularly sensitive to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate-68">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[65]</a></sup> Nevertheless, according to the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">2014 Environmental Performance Index</a>, Switzerland ranks first among 132 nations in safeguarding the environment, due to its high scores on environmental public health, its heavy reliance on renewable sources of energy (<a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geothermal" class="mw-redirect" title="Geothermal">geothermal</a> energy), and its control of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[66]</a></sup> In 2020 it was ranked third out of 180 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[67]</a></sup> The country pledged to cut <a href="/wiki/GHG_emissions" class="mw-redirect" title="GHG emissions">GHG emissions</a> by 50% by the year 2030 compared to the level of 1990 and works on a plan to reach zero emissions by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Switzerland is far lower than world average. In 2016, Switzerland had 1.0 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-GFN_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFN-75">[69]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, 40 percent less than world average of 1.6 global hectares per person. In contrast, in 2016, they used 4.6 global hectares of biocapacity - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they used about 4.6 times as much biocapacity as Switzerland contains. The remainder comes from imports and overusing the global commons (such as the atmosphere through greenhouse gas emissions). As a result, Switzerland is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-GFN_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GFN-75">[69]</a></sup> Switzerland had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 3.53/10, ranking it 150th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-76">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Switzerland" title="Politics of Switzerland">Politics of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg/220px-Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg/330px-Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg/440px-Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5615" data-file-height="3825"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundesrat_der_Schweiz_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Swiss Federal Council</a> in 2016 with President <a href="/wiki/Johann_Schneider-Ammann" title="Johann Schneider-Ammann">Johann Schneider-Ammann</a> (front, centre)<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[note 7]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Constitution" title="Swiss Federal Constitution">Federal Constitution</a> adopted in 1848 is the legal foundation of the modern federal state.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup> A new Swiss Constitution was adopted in 1999, but did not introduce notable changes to the federal structure. It outlines basic and political rights of individuals and citizen participation in public affairs, divides the powers between the Confederation and the cantons and defines federal jurisdiction and authority. There are three main governing bodies on the federal level:<sup id="cite_ref-Federalism_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Federalism-79">[72]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> parliament (legislative), the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Federal Council</a> (executive) and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland">Federal Court</a> (judicial). </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bundeshaus_Bern_2009,_Flooffy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg/170px-Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg/255px-Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg/340px-Bundeshaus_Bern_2009%2C_Flooffy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="843"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bundeshaus_Bern_2009,_Flooffy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Palace">Federal Palace</a>, seat of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Switzerland">Federal Assembly</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Federal Council</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Parliament">Swiss Parliament</a> consists of two houses: the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Council_of_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Council of States">Council of States</a> which has 46 representatives (two from each canton and one from each <a href="/wiki/Half-canton" class="mw-redirect" title="Half-canton">half-canton</a>) who are elected under a system determined by each canton, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="National Council of Switzerland">National Council</a>, which consists of 200 members who are elected under a system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>, depending on the population of each canton. Members of both houses serve for 4 years and only serve as members of parliament part-time (so-called <i>Milizsystem</i> or <a href="/wiki/Citizen_legislature" title="Citizen legislature">citizen legislature</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-urlMiliz-Parlamentswissinfo.ch_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urlMiliz-Parlamentswissinfo.ch-80">[73]</a></sup> When both houses are in joint session, they are known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Switzerland">Federal Assembly</a>. Through <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendums</a>, citizens may challenge any law passed by parliament and through <a href="/wiki/Initiative" title="Initiative">initiatives</a>, introduce amendments to the federal constitution, thus making Switzerland a <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Federal Council constitutes the federal government, directs the <a href="/wiki/Federal_administration_of_Switzerland" title="Federal administration of Switzerland">federal administration</a> and serves as collective <a href="/wiki/Head_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of State">Head of State</a>. It is a collegial body of seven members, elected for a four-year mandate by the Federal Assembly which also exercises <a href="/wiki/Regulation" title="Regulation">oversight</a> over the council. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Swiss_Confederation" title="President of the Swiss Confederation">President of the Confederation</a> is elected by the Assembly from among the seven members, traditionally in rotation and for a one-year term; the President chairs the government and assumes representative functions. However, the president is a <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i> with no additional powers, and remains the head of a department within the administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Swiss government has been a coalition of the four major political parties since 1959, each party having a number of seats that roughly reflects its share of electorate and representation in the federal parliament. The classic distribution of 2 CVP/PDC, 2 SPS/PSS, 2 FDP/PRD and 1 SVP/UDC as it stood from 1959 to 2003 was known as the "<a href="/wiki/Magic_formula" title="Magic formula">magic formula</a>". Following the <a href="/wiki/2015_Swiss_Federal_Council_election" title="2015 Swiss Federal Council election">2015 Federal Council elections</a>, the seven seats in the Federal Council were distributed as follows: </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        1 seat for the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_People%27s_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Christian Democratic People's Party of Switzerland">Christian Democratic People's Party (CVP/PDC)</a>,
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        2 seats for the <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Free Democratic Party of Switzerland">Free Democratic Party (FDP/PRD)</a>,
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        2 seats for the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Switzerland" title="Social Democratic Party of Switzerland">Social Democratic Party (SPS/PSS)</a>,
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        2 seats for the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">Swiss People's Party (SVP/UDC)</a>.
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p>The function of the Federal Supreme Court is to hear appeals against rulings of cantonal or federal courts. The judges are elected by the Federal Assembly for six-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-FederalCourts_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FederalCourts-81">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Direct_democracy">Direct democracy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Voting_in_Switzerland" title="Voting in Switzerland">Voting in Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg/220px-Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg/330px-Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg/440px-Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Landsgemeinde_Glarus_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Landsgemeinde" title="Landsgemeinde">Landsgemeinde</a> is an old form of <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a>, still in practice in two cantons.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">Direct democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a> are hallmarks of the Swiss political system.<sup id="cite_ref-CHPS_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHPS-82">[75]</a></sup> Swiss citizens are subject to three legal jurisdictions: the municipality, canton and federal levels. The 1848 and 1999 Swiss Constitutions define a system of direct democracy (sometimes called half-direct or representative direct democracy because it is aided by the more commonplace institutions of a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>). The instruments of this system at the federal level, known as popular rights (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Volksrechte</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">droits populaires</i>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">diritti popolari</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-PopularRights_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopularRights-83">[76]</a></sup> include the right to submit a federal initiative and a referendum, both of which may overturn parliamentary decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By calling a federal referendum, a group of citizens may challenge a law passed by parliament, if they gather 50,000 signatures against the law within 100 days. If so, a national vote is scheduled where voters decide by a <a href="/wiki/Majority" title="Majority">simple majority</a> whether to accept or reject the law. Any 8 cantons together can also call a constitutional referendum on a federal law.<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Similarly, the federal <i>constitutional initiative</i> allows citizens to put a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_amendment" title="Constitutional amendment">constitutional amendment</a> to a national vote, if 100,000 voters sign the proposed amendment within 18 months.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[note 8]</a></sup> The Federal Council and the Federal Assembly can supplement the proposed amendment with a counter-proposal, and then voters must indicate a preference on the ballot in case both proposals are accepted. Constitutional amendments, whether introduced by initiative or in parliament, must be accepted by a <a href="/wiki/Double_majority" title="Double majority">double majority</a> of the national popular vote and the cantonal popular votes.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[note 9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CHPS_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHPS-82">[75]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cantons">Cantons</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">Cantons of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Swiss Confederation consists of 26 cantons:<sup id="cite_ref-Politics_78-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Politics-78">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CHAuthorities_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHAuthorities-87">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table style="float:left; border:0; margin:2.6em 0 0;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg" class="image" title="Swiss cantons"><img alt="Swiss cantons" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg/500px-Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg.png" decoding="async" width="500" height="350" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg/750px-Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg/1000px-Kantone_der_Schweiz.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700"></a> </td>
        </tr>

         <td style="border-right:0;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Zug_matt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Zug matt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wappen_Zug_matt.svg/14px-Wappen_Zug_matt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wappen_Zug_matt.svg/21px-Wappen_Zug_matt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wappen_Zug_matt.svg/28px-Wappen_Zug_matt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="407" data-file-height="494"></a></td> 
         <td style="border-left:0;"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zug" title="Canton of Zug">Zug</a></td> 
         <td>9</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Zug" title="Zug">Zug</a> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="border-right:0;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Neuenburg matt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg/14px-Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg/21px-Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg/28px-Wappen_Neuenburg_matt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="493"></a></td> 
         <td style="border-left:0;"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Canton of Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a></td> 
         <td>24</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a></td> 
         <td style="border-right:0;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Zürich matt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg/14px-Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg.png" decoding="async" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg/21px-Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg/28px-Wappen_Z%C3%BCrich_matt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="492"></a></td> 
         <td style="border-left:0;"><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Canton of Zürich">Zürich</a></td> 
         <td>1</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>*<small>These cantons are known as half-cantons.</small> </p>
      <p>The cantons are <a href="/wiki/Federated_state" title="Federated state">federated states</a>, have a permanent constitutional status and, in comparison with the situation in other countries, a high degree of independence. Under the Federal Constitution, all 26 cantons are equal in status, except that 6 (referred to often as the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland#Half-cantons" title="Cantons of Switzerland">half-cantons</a>) are represented by only one councillor (instead of two) in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Council_of_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Council of States">Council of States</a> and have only half a cantonal vote with respect to the required cantonal majority in <a href="/wiki/Voting_in_Switzerland#Constitutional_referendums_(Popular_initiatives)" title="Voting in Switzerland">referendums on constitutional amendments</a>. Each canton has its own constitution, and its own parliament, government, police and courts.<sup id="cite_ref-CHAuthorities_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHAuthorities-87">[78]</a></sup> However, there are considerable differences between the individual cantons, most particularly in terms of population and geographical area. Their populations vary between 16,003 (Appenzell Innerrhoden) and 1,487,969 (Zürich), and their area between 37&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (14&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) (Basel-Stadt) and 7,105&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (2,743&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) (<a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Grisons" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton of Grisons">Grisons</a>). </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Switzerland" title="Municipalities of Switzerland">Municipalities of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The cantons comprise a total of 2,222 municipalities as of 2018. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_international_institutions">Foreign relations and international institutions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Switzerland" title="Foreign relations of Switzerland">Foreign relations of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditionally, Switzerland avoids alliances that might entail military, political, or direct economic action and has been neutral since the end of its <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_the_Old_Swiss_Confederacy" title="Growth of the Old Swiss Confederacy">expansion</a> in 1515. Its <a href="/wiki/Swiss_neutrality" title="Swiss neutrality">policy of neutrality</a> was internationally recognised at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> in 1815.<sup id="cite_ref-Neutrality_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutrality-88">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nationsencyclopedia.com_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationsencyclopedia.com-89">[80]</a></sup> Only in 2002 did Switzerland become a full member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a><sup id="cite_ref-Neutrality_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutrality-88">[79]</a></sup> and it was the first state to join it by <a href="/wiki/2002_Swiss_referendums" title="2002 Swiss referendums">referendum</a>. Switzerland maintains diplomatic relations with almost all countries and historically has served as an intermediary between other states.<sup id="cite_ref-Neutrality_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutrality-88">[79]</a></sup> Switzerland is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>; the Swiss people have consistently rejected membership since the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-Neutrality_88-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutrality-88">[79]</a></sup> However, Switzerland does participate in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[81]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Swiss_neutrality" title="Swiss neutrality">Swiss neutrality</a> has been questioned at times.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/170px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/255px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg/340px-Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Red_Cross.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Monochrome" title="Monochrome">monochromatically</a> reversed Swiss flag became the symbol of the Red Cross Movement,<sup id="cite_ref-FCO_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-60">[54]</a></sup> founded in 1863 by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Dunant" title="Henry Dunant">Henry Dunant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[87]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many international institutions have their seats in Switzerland, in part because of its policy of neutrality. <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> is the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a> and, since 2006, hosts the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a>. Even though Switzerland is one of the most recent countries to have joined the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations,_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Nations, Geneva">Palace of Nations</a> in Geneva is the second biggest centre for the United Nations after New York, and Switzerland was a founding member and home to the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. </p>
      <p>Apart from the United Nations headquarters, the Swiss Confederation is host to many UN agencies, like the World Health Organization (<a href="/wiki/WHO" class="mw-redirect" title="WHO">WHO</a>), the International Labour Organization (<a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">ILO</a>), the International Telecommunication Union (<a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">ITU</a>), the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UNHCR</a>) and about 200 other international organisations, including the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Organization" title="World Intellectual Property Organization">World Intellectual Property Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Neutrality_88-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neutrality-88">[79]</a></sup> The annual meetings of the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Davos" title="Davos">Davos</a> bring together top international business and political leaders from Switzerland and foreign countries to discuss important issues facing the world, including health and the environment. Additionally the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_for_International_Settlements" title="Bank for International Settlements">Bank for International Settlements</a> (BIS) are located in <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> since 1930. </p>
      <p>Furthermore, many sports federations and organisations are located throughout the country, such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Handball_Federation" title="International Handball Federation">International Handball Federation</a> in Basel, the <a href="/wiki/International_Basketball_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Basketball Federation">International Basketball Federation</a> in Geneva, the Union of European Football Associations (<a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Nyon" title="Nyon">Nyon</a>, the International Federation of Association Football (<a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/International_Ice_Hockey_Federation" title="International Ice Hockey Federation">International Ice Hockey Federation</a> both in <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Cycliste_Internationale" title="Union Cycliste Internationale">International Cycling Union</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aigle" title="Aigle">Aigle</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Armed_Forces" title="Swiss Armed Forces">Swiss Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Swiss_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontifical Swiss Guard">Pontifical Swiss Guard</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg/170px-Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg/255px-Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg/340px-Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="661" data-file-height="992"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Switzerland_-_Air_Force_McDonnell_Douglas_FA-18C_Hornet_-_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Swiss Air Force <a href="/wiki/F/A-18_Hornet" class="mw-redirect" title="F/A-18 Hornet">F/A-18 Hornet</a> at <a href="/wiki/Axalp_Air_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Axalp Air Show">Axalp Air Show</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Armed_Forces" title="Swiss Armed Forces">Swiss Armed Forces</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Ground_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Ground Forces">Land Forces</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Air_Force" title="Swiss Air Force">Air Force</a>, are <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_Switzerland" title="Conscription in Switzerland">composed</a> mostly of conscripts, male citizens aged from 20 to 34 (in special cases up to 50) years. Being a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> country, Switzerland has no navy; however, on lakes bordering neighbouring countries, armed military patrol boats are used. Swiss citizens are prohibited from serving in foreign armies, except for the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Swiss_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontifical Swiss Guard">Swiss Guards</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a>, or if they are <a href="/wiki/Dual_citizen" class="mw-redirect" title="Dual citizen">dual citizens</a> of a foreign country and reside there. </p>
      <p>The structure of the Swiss militia system stipulates that the soldiers keep their Army issued equipment, including all personal weapons, at home. Some organisations and political parties find this practice controversial.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[89]</a></sup> Women can serve voluntarily. Men usually receive military conscription orders for training at the age of 18.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[90]</a></sup> About two thirds of the young Swiss are found suited for service; for those found unsuited, various forms of alternative service exist.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[91]</a></sup> Annually, approximately 20,000 persons are trained in recruit centres for a duration from 18 to 21 weeks. The reform "Army XXI" was adopted by popular vote in 2003, it replaced the previous model "Army 95", reducing the effectiveness from 400,000 to about 200,000. Of those, 120,000 are active in periodic Army training and 80,000 are non-training reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The newest reform of the military, WEA/DEVA/USEs, started in 2019 and will reduce the number of army personnel progressively to 100,000 by the end of 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg/220px-SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg/330px-SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg/440px-SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2652" data-file-height="1572"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:SKdt-Fahrzeug_-_Schweizer_Armee_-_Steel_Parade_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Swiss-built <a href="/wiki/Mowag_Eagle" title="Mowag Eagle">Mowag Eagles</a> of the Land Forces
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Overall, three general mobilisations have been declared to ensure the integrity and neutrality of Switzerland. The first one was held on the occasion of the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> of 1870–71. The second was in response to the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a> in August 1914. The third mobilisation of the army took place in September 1939 in response to the <a href="/wiki/German_attack_on_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="German attack on Poland">German attack on Poland</a>; <a href="/wiki/Henri_Guisan" title="Henri Guisan">Henri Guisan</a> was elected as the General-in-Chief. </p>
      <p>Because of its neutrality policy, the Swiss army does not currently take part in armed conflicts in other countries but is part of some peacekeeping missions around the world. Since 2000 the armed force department has also maintained the <a href="/wiki/Onyx_(interception_system)" title="Onyx (interception system)">Onyx</a> intelligence gathering system to monitor satellite communications.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[94]</a></sup> Switzerland decided not to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Nuclear Weapon Ban Treaty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> there have been a number of attempts to curb military activity or even abolish the armed forces altogether. A notable referendum on the subject, launched by an <a href="/wiki/Group_for_a_Switzerland_without_an_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Group for a Switzerland without an Army">anti-militarist group</a>, was held on 26 November 1989. It was defeated with about two-thirds of the voters against the proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[97]</a></sup> A similar referendum, called for before, but held shortly after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September attacks</a> in the US, was defeated by over 78% of voters.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Gun_politics_in_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Gun politics in Switzerland">Gun politics in Switzerland</a> are unique in Europe in that 2–3.5 million guns are in the hands of civilians, giving the nation an estimate of 27.6–41.2 guns per 100 people.<sup id="cite_ref-gunpolicy.org_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gunpolicy.org-108">[99]</a></sup> It is worth noting that as per Small Arms Survey, only 324,484 guns are owned by the military on top of the civilian-owned ones,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[100]</a></sup> but that only 143,372 are in the hands of soldiers as per Army numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[101]</a></sup> However, ammunition is no longer issued.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_capital_or_Federal_City_issue">The capital or Federal City issue</span></h3> 
      <p>Until 1848 the rather loosely coupled Confederation did not know a central political organisation, but representatives, mayors, and <i>Landammänner</i> met several times a year at the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland"><i>Lieu</i></a> presiding the <a href="/wiki/Tagsatzung" title="Tagsatzung">Confederal Diet</a> for one year. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bern_007_(35250800705).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg/220px-Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg/330px-Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg/440px-Bern_007_%2835250800705%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2992"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bern_007_(35250800705).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Old_City_of_Bern" class="mw-redirect" title="Old City of Bern">Old City of Bern</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Until 1500 the legates met most of the time in <a href="/wiki/Lucerne" title="Lucerne">Lucerne</a>, but also in Zürich, <a href="/wiki/Baden" title="Baden">Baden</a>, Bern, Schwyz etc., but sometimes also at places outside of the confederation, such as <a href="/wiki/Constance" class="mw-redirect" title="Constance">Constance</a>. From the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_War" title="Swabian War">Swabian War</a> in 1499 onwards until Reformation, most conferences met in Zurich. Afterwards, the town hall at Baden, where the annual accounts of the common people had been held regularly since 1426, became the most frequent, but not the sole place of assembly. After 1712 <a href="/wiki/Frauenfeld" title="Frauenfeld">Frauenfeld</a> gradually dissolved Baden. From 1526, the Catholic conferences were held mostly in Lucerne, the Protestant conferences from 1528 mostly in <a href="/wiki/Aarau" title="Aarau">Aarau</a>, the one for the legitimation of the French Ambassador in <a href="/wiki/Solothurn" title="Solothurn">Solothurn</a>. At the same time the syndicate for the <i>Ennetbirgischen Vogteien</i> located in the present Ticino met from 1513 in <a href="/wiki/Lugano" title="Lugano">Lugano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Locarno" title="Locarno">Locarno</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HDSdiet_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDSdiet-113">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Helvetic_Republic" title="Helvetic Republic">Helvetic Republic</a> and during the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Mediation" title="Act of Mediation">Mediation</a> from 1803 until 1815 the Confederal Diet of the 19 <i>Lieus</i> met at the capitals of the <i>directoral cantons</i> <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">Fribourg</a>, Berne, <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Basel-City" class="mw-redirect" title="Canton of Basel-City">Basel</a>, Zurich, Lucerne and Solothurn.<sup id="cite_ref-HDSdiet_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDSdiet-113">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After the Long Diet from 6 April 1814 to 31 August 1815 took place in Zurich to replace the constitution and the enhancement of the Confederation to 22 cantons by the admission of the cantons of Valais, Neuchâtel and Geneva to full members, the directorial cantons of Lucerne, Zurich and Berne took over the diet in two-year turns.<sup id="cite_ref-HDSdiet_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDSdiet-113">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1848, the federal constitution provided that details concerning the federal institutions, such as their locations, should be taken care of by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Switzerland">Federal Assembly</a> (BV 1848 Art. 108). Thus on 28 November 1848, the Federal Assembly voted in majority to locate the seat of government in Berne. And, as a prototypical federal compromise, to assign other federal institutions, such as the <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">Federal Polytechnical School</a> (1854, the later ETH) to Zurich, and other institutions to Lucerne, such as the later <a href="/wiki/SUVA" class="mw-redirect" title="SUVA">SUVA</a> (1912) and the Federal Insurance Court (1917). In 1875, a law (RS 112) fixed the compensations owed by the city of Bern for the federal seat.<sup id="cite_ref-Bundesstadt_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bundesstadt-2">[1]</a></sup> According to these living fundamental federalistic feelings further federal institutions were subsequently attributed to <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a> (<a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland">Federal Supreme Court</a> in 1872, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Polytechnique_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_Lausanne" title="École Polytechnique Fédérale de Lausanne">EPFL</a> in 1969), <a href="/wiki/Bellinzona" title="Bellinzona">Bellinzona</a> (<a href="/wiki/Federal_Criminal_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Criminal Court of Switzerland">Federal Criminal Court</a>, 2004), and <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen" title="St. Gallen">St. Gallen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_(Switzerland)" title="Federal Administrative Court (Switzerland)">Federal Administrative Court</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federal_Patent_Court_(Switzerland)" title="Federal Patent Court (Switzerland)">Federal Patent Court</a>, 2012). </p>
      <p>The 1999 new constitution, however, does not contain anything concerning any Federal City. In 2002 a tripartite committee has been asked by the Swiss Federal Council to prepare the "creation of a federal law on the status of Bern as a Federal City", and to evaluate the positive and negative aspects for the city and the canton of Bern if this status were awarded. After a first report, the work of this committee was suspended in 2004 by the Swiss Federal Council, and work on this subject has not resumed since.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Thus as of today, no city in Switzerland has the official status either of capital or of Federal City, nevertheless, Bern is commonly referred to as "Federal City" (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Bundesstadt</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">ville fédérale</i>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">città federale</i>). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_labour_law">Economy and labour law</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Switzerland" title="Economy of Switzerland">Economy of Switzerland</a>
      </div>

      </div>

         <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
