        <tr> 
         <th scope="row"><b><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religious affiliation</a></b> </th> 
         <td>26.3 </td> 
         <td align="left"><span style="display:none;">26.3</span>
          <div style="width:78.9px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:#A57164">
           &nbsp;
          </div> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <th scope="row">unknown </th> 
         <td>1.4 </td> 
         <td align="left"><span style="display:none;">1.4</span>
          <div style="width:4.2px;height:2ex;background:#aaa;background:grey">
           &nbsp;
          </div> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Switzerland has no official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>, though most of the <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Switzerland" title="Cantons of Switzerland">cantons</a> (except <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Geneva" title="Canton of Geneva">Geneva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Canton of Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a>) recognise official churches, which are either the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Switzerland">Roman Catholic Church</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Reformed_Church" title="Swiss Reformed Church">Swiss Reformed Church</a>. These churches, and in some cantons also the <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic_Church" title="Old Catholic Church">Old Catholic Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> congregations, are financed by official taxation of adherents.<sup id="cite_ref-CHKirchenSteuer_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHKirchenSteuer-241">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the predominant religion of Switzerland (about 67% of resident population in 2016-2018<sup id="cite_ref-SFOReligions_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFOReligions-5">[4]</a></sup> and 75% of Swiss citizens<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[231]</a></sup>), divided between the Roman Catholic Church (35.8% of the population), the Swiss Reformed Church (23.8%), further <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches (2.2%), <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (2.5%), and other Christian denominations (2.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-SFOReligions_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFOReligions-5">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Switzerland" title="Immigration to Switzerland">Immigration</a> has established <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (5.3%) as a sizeable minority religion.<sup id="cite_ref-SFOReligions_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFOReligions-5">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>26.3% of Swiss permanent residents are not affiliated with any religious community (<a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">Agnosticism</a>, and others).<sup id="cite_ref-SFOReligions_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SFOReligions-5">[4]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of the 2000 census other Christian minority communities included Neo-<a href="/wiki/Pietism" title="Pietism">Pietism</a> (0.44%), <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">Pentecostalism</a> (0.28%, mostly incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/Schweizer_Pfingstmission" class="mw-redirect" title="Schweizer Pfingstmission">Schweizer Pfingstmission</a>), <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a> (0.13%), the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a> (0.45%), <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.28%), other Protestant denominations (0.20%), the <a href="/wiki/Old_Catholic_Church" title="Old Catholic Church">Old Catholic Church</a> (0.18%), other Christian denominations (0.20%). Non-Christian religions are <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (0.38%), <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.29%), <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> (0.25%) and others (0.11%); 4.3% did not make a statement.<sup id="cite_ref-CHReligion2000_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHReligion2000-243">[232]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country was historically about evenly balanced between Catholic and Protestant, with a complex patchwork of majorities over most of the country. Switzerland <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Switzerland" title="Reformation in Switzerland">played an exceptional role</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> as it became home to many <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformers" title="Protestant Reformers">reformers</a>. <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a> converted to Protestantism in 1536, just before <a href="/wiki/John_Calvin" title="John Calvin">John Calvin</a> arrived there. In 1541, he founded the <i><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Geneva" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Geneva">Republic of Geneva</a></i> on his own ideals. It became known internationally as the <i>Protestant Rome</i>, and housed such reformers as <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Beza" title="Theodore Beza">Theodore Beza</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Farel" title="William Farel">William Farel</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Viret" title="Pierre Viret">Pierre Viret</a>. <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a> <a href="/wiki/Reformation_in_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Reformation in Zürich">became</a> another stronghold around the same time, with <a href="/wiki/Huldrych_Zwingli" title="Huldrych Zwingli">Huldrych Zwingli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Bullinger" title="Heinrich Bullinger">Heinrich Bullinger</a> taking the lead there. Anabaptists <a href="/wiki/Felix_Manz" title="Felix Manz">Felix Manz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Grebel" title="Conrad Grebel">Conrad Grebel</a> also operated there. They were later joined by the fleeing <a href="/wiki/Peter_Martyr_Vermigli" title="Peter Martyr Vermigli">Peter Martyr Vermigli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hans_Denck" title="Hans Denck">Hans Denck</a>. Other centres included <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> (<a href="/wiki/Andreas_Karlstadt" title="Andreas Karlstadt">Andreas Karlstadt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Oecolampadius" title="Johannes Oecolampadius">Johannes Oecolampadius</a>), <a href="/wiki/Berne" class="mw-redirect" title="Berne">Berne</a> (<a href="/wiki/Berchtold_Haller" title="Berchtold Haller">Berchtold Haller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niklaus_Manuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Niklaus Manuel">Niklaus Manuel</a>), and <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen" title="St. Gallen">St. Gallen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Joachim_Vadian" title="Joachim Vadian">Joachim Vadian</a>). One canton, Appenzell, was officially divided into Catholic and Protestant sections in 1597. The larger cities and their cantons (Bern, Geneva, Lausanne, Zürich and Basel) used to be predominantly Protestant. <a href="/wiki/Central_Switzerland" title="Central Switzerland">Central Switzerland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Valais" title="Valais">Valais</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ticino" title="Ticino">Ticino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Appenzell_Innerrhoden" title="Appenzell Innerrhoden">Appenzell Innerrhodes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Jura" title="Canton of Jura">Jura</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Fribourg" title="Canton of Fribourg">Fribourg</a> are traditionally Catholic. The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Constitution">Swiss Constitution</a> of 1848, under the recent impression of the clashes of Catholic vs. Protestant cantons that culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Sonderbundskrieg" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonderbundskrieg">Sonderbundskrieg</a>, consciously defines a <a href="/wiki/Consociational_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Consociational state">consociational state</a>, allowing the peaceful co-existence of Catholics and Protestants. A 1980 initiative calling for the complete <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a> was rejected by 78.9% of the voters.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[233]</a></sup> Some traditionally Protestant cantons and cities nowadays have a slight Catholic majority, not because they were growing in members, quite the contrary, but only because since about 1970 a steadily growing minority became not affiliated with any church or other religious body (21.4% in Switzerland, 2012) especially in traditionally Protestant regions, such as Basel-City (42%), canton of Neuchâtel (38%), canton of Geneva (35%), canton of Vaud (26%), or Zürich city (city: &gt;25%; canton: 23%).<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[234]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Switzerland" title="Culture of Switzerland">Culture of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Switzerland" title="Music of Switzerland">Music of Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_folklore" title="Swiss folklore">Swiss folklore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alpine_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine culture">Alpine culture</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vals06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Vals06.JPG/220px-Vals06.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Vals06.JPG/330px-Vals06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Vals06.JPG/440px-Vals06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vals06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Alphorn" title="Alphorn">Alphorn</a> concert in <a href="/wiki/Vals,_Switzerland" title="Vals, Switzerland">Vals</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Three of Europe's major languages are official in Switzerland. Swiss culture is characterised by diversity, which is reflected in a wide range of traditional customs.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[235]</a></sup> A region may be in some ways strongly culturally connected to the neighbouring country that shares its language, the country itself being rooted in western <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">European culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[236]</a></sup> The linguistically isolated <a href="/wiki/Romansh_language" title="Romansh language">Romansh</a> culture in <a href="/wiki/Graub%C3%BCnden" class="mw-redirect" title="Graubünden">Graubünden</a> in eastern Switzerland constitutes an exception, it survives only in the upper valleys of the Rhine and the Inn and strives to maintain its rare linguistic tradition. </p>
      <p>Switzerland is home to many notable contributors to literature, art, architecture, music and sciences. In addition the country attracted a number of creative persons during time of unrest or war in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[237]</a></sup> Some 1000 museums are distributed through the country; the number has more than tripled since 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[238]</a></sup> Among the most important cultural performances held annually are the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A9o_Festival" title="Paléo Festival">Paléo Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucerne_Festival" title="Lucerne Festival">Lucerne Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[239]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Montreux_Jazz_Festival" title="Montreux Jazz Festival">Montreux Jazz Festival</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[240]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Locarno_International_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Locarno International Film Festival">Locarno International Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Art_Basel" title="Art Basel">Art Basel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[241]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Alpine symbolism has played an essential role in shaping the history of the country and the Swiss national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-j1_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-j1-21">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[242]</a></sup> Many alpine areas and <a href="/wiki/Ski_resort" title="Ski resort">ski resorts</a> offer <a href="/wiki/Winter_sports" title="Winter sports">winter sports</a> during the colder months as well as <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">das Wandern</i>) or <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">Mountain biking</a> in summer. Other areas throughout the year have a recreational culture that caters to tourism such as sightseeing, yet the quieter seasons are spring and autumn when there are fewer visitors. A traditional farmer and herder culture also predominates in many areas and small farms are omnipresent outside the towns. Folk art is kept alive in organisations all over the country. In Switzerland, it is mostly expressed in music, dance, poetry, wood carving and embroidery. The <a href="/wiki/Alphorn" title="Alphorn">alphorn</a>, a trumpet-like musical instrument made of wood, has become alongside <a href="/wiki/Yodel" class="mw-redirect" title="Yodel">yodeling</a> and the accordion an epitome of traditional <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Switzerland" title="Music of Switzerland">Swiss music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[244]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Switzerland">Literature of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_(painted_portrait).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg/170px-Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg/255px-Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg/340px-Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_%28painted_portrait%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1448" data-file-height="2016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Jean-Jacques_Rousseau_(painted_portrait).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a> was not only a writer but also an influential philosopher of the eighteenth century.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[245]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As the Confederation, from its foundation in 1291, was almost exclusively composed of German-speaking regions, the earliest forms of literature are in German. In the 18th century, French became the fashionable language in Bern and elsewhere, while the influence of the French-speaking allies and subject lands was more marked than before.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[246]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the classic authors of Swiss German literature are <a href="/wiki/Jeremias_Gotthelf" title="Jeremias Gotthelf">Jeremias Gotthelf</a> (1797–1854) and <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Keller" title="Gottfried Keller">Gottfried Keller</a> (1819–1890). The undisputed giants of 20th-century Swiss literature are <a href="/wiki/Max_Frisch" title="Max Frisch">Max Frisch</a> (1911–91) and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_D%C3%BCrrenmatt" title="Friedrich Dürrenmatt">Friedrich Dürrenmatt</a> (1921–90), whose repertoire includes <i>Die Physiker</i> (<a href="/wiki/The_Physicists" title="The Physicists">The Physicists</a>) and <i>Das Versprechen</i> (<a href="/wiki/The_Pledge:_Requiem_for_the_Detective_Novel" title="The Pledge: Requiem for the Detective Novel">The Pledge</a>), released in 2001 as a Hollywood film.<sup id="cite_ref-Literature_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Literature-258">[247]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Famous French-speaking writers were <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a> (1712–1778) and <a href="/wiki/Germaine_de_Sta%C3%ABl" title="Germaine de Staël">Germaine de Staël</a> (1766–1817). More recent authors include <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ferdinand_Ramuz" title="Charles Ferdinand Ramuz">Charles Ferdinand Ramuz</a> (1878–1947), whose novels describe the lives of peasants and mountain dwellers, set in a harsh environment and <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Cendrars" title="Blaise Cendrars">Blaise Cendrars</a> (born Frédéric Sauser, 1887–1961).<sup id="cite_ref-Literature_258-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Literature-258">[247]</a></sup> Italian and Romansh-speaking authors also contributed to the Swiss literary landscape, but generally in more modest ways given their small number. </p>
      <p>Probably the most famous Swiss literary creation, <i><a href="/wiki/Heidi" title="Heidi">Heidi</a></i>, the story of an orphan girl who lives with her grandfather in the Alps, is one of the most popular children's books ever and has come to be a symbol of Switzerland. Her creator, <a href="/wiki/Johanna_Spyri" title="Johanna Spyri">Johanna Spyri</a> (1827–1901), wrote a number of other books on similar themes.<sup id="cite_ref-Literature_258-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Literature-258">[247]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Switzerland">Media of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The freedom of the press and the right to free expression is guaranteed in the federal constitution of Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-259">[248]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Schweizerische_Depeschenagentur" class="mw-redirect" title="Schweizerische Depeschenagentur">Swiss News Agency</a> (SNA) broadcasts information around-the-clock in three of the four national languages—on politics, economics, society and culture. The SNA supplies almost all Swiss media and a couple of dozen foreign media services with its news.<sup id="cite_ref-Media_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Media-259">[248]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Switzerland has historically boasted the greatest number of newspaper titles published in proportion to its population and size.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-260">[249]</a></sup> The most influential newspapers are the German-language <i><a href="/wiki/Tages-Anzeiger" title="Tages-Anzeiger">Tages-Anzeiger</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Neue_Z%C3%BCrcher_Zeitung" title="Neue Zürcher Zeitung">Neue Zürcher Zeitung</a></i> NZZ, and the French-language <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Temps" title="Le Temps">Le Temps</a></i>, but almost every city has at least one local newspaper. The cultural diversity accounts for a variety of newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-260">[249]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government exerts greater control over broadcast media than print media, especially due to finance and licensing.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_260-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-260">[249]</a></sup> The Swiss Broadcasting Corporation, whose name was recently changed to <a href="/wiki/SRG_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="SRG SSR">SRG SSR</a>, is charged with the production and broadcast of radio and television programmes. SRG SSR studios are distributed throughout the various language regions. Radio content is produced in six central and four regional studios while the television programmes are produced in <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lugano" title="Lugano">Lugano</a>. An extensive cable network also allows most Swiss to access the programmes from neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Press_260-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Press-260">[249]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Switzerland" title="Sport in Switzerland">Sport in Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG/220px-Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG/330px-Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG/440px-Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Allalinhorn_4027_2007_04_17.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ski area over the glaciers of <a href="/wiki/Saas-Fee" title="Saas-Fee">Saas-Fee</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">Skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mountaineering" title="Mountaineering">mountaineering</a> are among the most popular sports in Switzerland, the nature of the country being particularly suited for such activities.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[250]</a></sup> Winter sports are practised by the natives and tourists since the second half of the 19th century with the invention of <a href="/wiki/Bobsleigh" title="Bobsleigh">bobsleigh</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Moritz" title="St. Moritz">St. Moritz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[251]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/FIS_Alpine_World_Ski_Championships" title="FIS Alpine World Ski Championships">world ski championships</a> were held in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCrren" title="Mürren">Mürren</a> (1931) and St. Moritz (1934). The latter town hosted the second <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a> in 1928 and the fifth edition in 1948. Among the most successful skiers and world champions are <a href="/wiki/Pirmin_Zurbriggen" title="Pirmin Zurbriggen">Pirmin Zurbriggen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Didier_Cuche" title="Didier Cuche">Didier Cuche</a>. </p>
      <p>The most prominently watched sports in Switzerland are <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Switzerland" title="Football in Switzerland">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schweizerischer_Eishockeyverband" class="mw-redirect" title="Schweizerischer Eishockeyverband">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIS_Alpine_World_Ski_Championships" title="FIS Alpine World Ski Championships">Alpine skiing</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Schwingen" title="Schwingen">Schwingen</a>", and <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The headquarters of the international football's and ice hockey's governing bodies, the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="International Federation of Association Football">International Federation of Association Football (FIFA)</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Ice_Hockey_Federation" title="International Ice Hockey Federation">International Ice Hockey Federation (IIHF)</a>, are located in Zürich. Many other headquarters of international sports federations are located in Switzerland. For example, the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee (IOC)</a>, IOC's <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Museum" title="Olympic Museum">Olympic Museum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Arbitration_for_Sport" title="Court of Arbitration for Sport">Court of Arbitration for Sport (CAS)</a> are located in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a>. </p>
      <p>Switzerland hosted the <a href="/wiki/1954_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1954 FIFA World Cup">1954 FIFA World Cup</a>, and was the joint host, with Austria, of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a> tournament. The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">Swiss Super League</a> is the nation's professional football club league. Europe's highest football pitch, at 2,000 metres (6,600&nbsp;ft) above sea level, is located in Switzerland and is named the <i>Ottmar Hitzfeld Stadium</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[253]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_(26_June_2009,_Wimbledon)_2_new.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg/170px-Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="348" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg/255px-Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg/340px-Roger_Federer_%2826_June_2009%2C_Wimbledon%29_2_new.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1316" data-file-height="2695"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Roger_Federer_(26_June_2009,_Wimbledon)_2_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> has won a record 20 Grand Slam singles titles, making him the most successful men's tennis player ever.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[254]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Many Swiss also follow <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> and support one of the 12 teams of the <a href="/wiki/National_League_A" class="mw-redirect" title="National League A">National League</a>, which is the most attended league in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[255]</a></sup> In 2009, Switzerland hosted the <a href="/wiki/2009_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2009 IIHF World Championship">IIHF World Championship</a> for the 10th time.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[256]</a></sup> It also became <a href="/wiki/2013_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2013 IIHF World Championship">World Vice-Champion</a> in 2013 and 2018. The numerous lakes make Switzerland an attractive place for sailing. The largest, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a>, is the home of the sailing team <a href="/wiki/Alinghi" title="Alinghi">Alinghi</a> which was the first European team to win the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America's Cup">America's Cup</a> in 2003 and which successfully defended the title in 2007. </p>
      <p>Swiss tennis player <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> is widely regarded as one of the greatest tennis players of all time. He has won 20 <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">Grand Slam</a> tournaments overall including a record 8 <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon</a> titles. He has also won a record 6 <a href="/wiki/ATP_Finals" title="ATP Finals">ATP Finals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20_Grand_Slams_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20_Grand_Slams-268">[257]</a></sup> He was ranked no. 1 in the <a href="/wiki/ATP_Rankings" title="ATP Rankings">ATP Rankings</a> for a record 237 consecutive weeks. He ended <a href="/wiki/2004_ATP_Tour" title="2004 ATP Tour">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_ATP_Tour" title="2005 ATP Tour">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_ATP_Tour" title="2006 ATP Tour">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_ATP_Tour" title="2007 ATP Tour">2007</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_ATP_World_Tour" title="2009 ATP World Tour">2009</a> ranked no. 1. Fellow swiss tennis stars <a href="/wiki/Martina_Hingis" title="Martina Hingis">Martina Hingis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stan_Wawrinka" title="Stan Wawrinka">Stan Wawrinka</a> also hold multiple Grand Slam titles. Switzerland won the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> title in <a href="/wiki/2014_Davis_Cup" title="2014 Davis Cup">2014</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">Motorsport</a> racecourses and events were banned in Switzerland following the <a href="/wiki/1955_Le_Mans_disaster" title="1955 Le Mans disaster">1955 Le Mans disaster</a> with exception to events such as <a href="/wiki/Hillclimbing" title="Hillclimbing">Hillclimbing</a>. During this period, the country still produced successful racing drivers such as <a href="/wiki/Clay_Regazzoni" title="Clay Regazzoni">Clay Regazzoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Buemi" title="Sébastien Buemi">Sébastien Buemi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo_Siffert" title="Jo Siffert">Jo Siffert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominique_Aegerter" title="Dominique Aegerter">Dominique Aegerter</a>, successful <a href="/wiki/World_Touring_Car_Championship" title="World Touring Car Championship">World Touring Car Championship</a> driver <a href="/wiki/Alain_Menu" title="Alain Menu">Alain Menu</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2014 24 Hours of Le Mans">2014 24 Hours of Le Mans</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Marcel_F%C3%A4ssler_(racing_driver)" title="Marcel Fässler (racing driver)">Marcel Fässler</a> and 2015 <a href="/wiki/24_Hours_N%C3%BCrburgring" class="mw-redirect" title="24 Hours Nürburgring">24 Hours Nürburgring</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Nico_M%C3%BCller" title="Nico Müller">Nico Müller</a>. <a href="/wiki/A1_Team_Switzerland" title="A1 Team Switzerland">Switzerland</a> also won the <a href="/wiki/A1_Grand_Prix" title="A1 Grand Prix">A1GP World Cup of Motorsport</a> in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_A1_Grand_Prix_season" title="2007–08 A1 Grand Prix season">2007–08</a> with driver <a href="/wiki/Neel_Jani" title="Neel Jani">Neel Jani</a>. Swiss <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_racer" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorcycle racer">motorcycle racer</a> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_L%C3%BCthi" title="Thomas Lüthi">Thomas Lüthi</a> won the 2005 <a href="/wiki/MotoGP" class="mw-redirect" title="MotoGP">MotoGP</a> World Championship in the 125cc category. In June 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_National_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss National Council">Swiss National Council</a>, one house of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Switzerland" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Switzerland">Federal Assembly of Switzerland</a>, voted to overturn the ban, however the other house, the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Council_of_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Council of States">Swiss Council of States</a> rejected the change and the ban remains in place.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Traditional sports include Swiss wrestling or "<a href="/wiki/Schwingen" title="Schwingen">Schwingen</a>". It is an old tradition from the rural central cantons and considered the national sport by some. <a href="/wiki/Hornussen" title="Hornussen">Hornussen</a> is another indigenous Swiss sport, which is like a cross between baseball and golf.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[260]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steinstossen" title="Steinstossen">Steinstossen</a> is the Swiss variant of <a href="/wiki/Stone_put" title="Stone put">stone put</a>, a competition in throwing a heavy stone. Practised only among the alpine population since <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric times</a>, it is recorded to have taken place in <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a> in the 13th century. It is also central to the <a href="/wiki/Unspunnenfest" title="Unspunnenfest">Unspunnenfest</a>, first held in 1805, with its symbol the 83.5 stone named <i>Unspunnenstein</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[261]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Swiss_cuisine" title="Swiss cuisine">Swiss cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Culinary_Heritage_of_Switzerland" title="Culinary Heritage of Switzerland">Culinary Heritage of Switzerland</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG/220px-Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG/330px-Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG/440px-Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="559"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Full_cheese_fondue_set_-_in_Switzerland.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Fondue" title="Fondue">Fondue</a> is melted cheese, into which bread is dipped.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The cuisine of Switzerland is multifaceted. While some dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Fondue" title="Fondue">fondue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raclette" title="Raclette">raclette</a> or <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B6sti" title="Rösti">rösti</a> are omnipresent through the country, each region developed its own gastronomy according to the differences of climate and languages.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[263]</a></sup> Traditional Swiss cuisine uses ingredients similar to those in other European countries, as well as unique <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheese" title="Cheese">cheeses</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Gruy%C3%A8re_(cheese)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gruyère (cheese)">Gruyère</a> or <a href="/wiki/Emmental_(cheese)" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmental (cheese)">Emmental</a>, produced in the valleys of <a href="/wiki/Gruy%C3%A8res" title="Gruyères">Gruyères</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emmental" title="Emmental">Emmental</a>. The number of fine-dining establishments is high, particularly in western Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[265]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Swiss_chocolate" title="Swiss chocolate">Chocolate</a> has been made in Switzerland since the 18th century but it gained its reputation at the end of the 19th century with the invention of modern techniques such as <a href="/wiki/Conching" title="Conching">conching</a> and <a href="/wiki/Why_Chocolate_Melts" class="mw-redirect" title="Why Chocolate Melts">tempering</a> which enabled its production on a high-quality level. Also a breakthrough was the invention of solid milk chocolate in 1875 by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Peter" title="Daniel Peter">Daniel Peter</a>. The Swiss are the world's largest consumers of chocolate.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[267]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to the popularisation of <a href="/wiki/Processed_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Processed food">processed foods</a> at the end of the 19th century, Swiss <a href="/wiki/Whole_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Whole food">health food</a> pioneer <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Bircher-Benner" title="Maximilian Bircher-Benner">Maximilian Bircher-Benner</a> created the first nutrition-based therapy in form of the well-known <a href="/wiki/Rolled_oats" title="Rolled oats">rolled oats</a> <a href="/wiki/Cereal" title="Cereal">cereal</a> dish, called <a href="/wiki/Muesli" title="Muesli">Birchermüesli</a>. </p>
      <p>The most popular alcoholic drink in Switzerland is wine. Switzerland is notable for the variety of grapes grown because of the large variations in <a href="/wiki/Terroir" title="Terroir">terroirs</a>, with their specific mixes of soil, air, altitude and light. <a href="/wiki/Swiss_wine" title="Swiss wine">Swiss wine</a> is produced mainly in <a href="/wiki/Valais_(wine_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valais (wine region)">Valais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vaud" title="Vaud">Vaud</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lavaux" title="Lavaux">Lavaux</a>), <a href="/wiki/Geneva_(wine_region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Geneva (wine region)">Geneva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ticino_(wine_region)" title="Ticino (wine region)">Ticino</a>, with a small majority of white wines. Vineyards have been cultivated in Switzerland since the Roman era, even though certain traces can be found of a more ancient origin. The most widespread varieties are the <a href="/wiki/Chasselas" title="Chasselas">Chasselas</a> (called <a href="/wiki/Fendant" class="mw-redirect" title="Fendant">Fendant</a> in Valais) and <a href="/wiki/Pinot_noir" title="Pinot noir">Pinot noir</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Merlot" title="Merlot">Merlot</a> is the main variety produced in Ticino.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[269]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes_and_references">Notes and references</span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-fedcit-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fedcit_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fedcit_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Bern is referred to as "federal city" (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Bundesstadt</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">ville fédérale</i>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">città federale</i>). Swiss law does not designate a <i>capital</i> as such, but the federal parliament and government are located in Bern, while the federal courts are located in other cities.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The original date of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCtlischwur" title="Rütlischwur">Rütlischwur</a> was 1307 (reported by <a href="/wiki/Aegidius_Tschudi" title="Aegidius Tschudi">Aegidius Tschudi</a> in the 16th century) and is just one among several comparable treaties between more or less the same parties during that period. The date of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Charter_of_1291" title="Federal Charter of 1291">Federal Charter of 1291</a> was selected in 1891 for the official celebration of the "Confederacy's 600th anniversary".</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A solemn declaration of the <a href="/wiki/Tagsatzung" title="Tagsatzung">Tagsatzung</a> declared the Federal Constitution adopted on 12 September 1848. A resolution of the <i>Tagsatzung</i> of 14 September 1848 specified that the powers of the institutions provided for by the 1815 Federal Treaty would expire at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">constitution</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Federal_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Federal Council">Federal Council</a>, which took place on 16 November 1848.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are several definitions. See <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Switzerland#Western_or_Central_Europe?" title="Geography of Switzerland">Geography of Switzerland#Western or Central Europe?</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Swiss_Standard_German" title="Swiss Standard German">Swiss Standard German</a> spelling and pronunciation. The <a href="/wiki/Swiss_German" title="Swiss German">Swiss German</a> name is sometimes spelled as <i>Schwyz</i> or <i>Schwiiz</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Alemannic_German" title="Help:IPA/Alemannic German">[ˈʃʋiːt͡s]</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Schwyz" title="Canton of Schwyz">Schwyz</a></i> is also the standard German (and international) name of one of the Swiss cantons.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The latter is the common <a href="/wiki/Sursilvan_dialects_(Romansh)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sursilvan dialects (Romansh)">Sursilvan</a> pronunciation.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As shown in this image, the current members of the council are (as of January 2016, from left to right): Federal Councillor <a href="/wiki/Alain_Berset" title="Alain Berset">Alain Berset</a>, Federal Councillor <a href="/wiki/Didier_Burkhalter" title="Didier Burkhalter">Didier Burkhalter</a>, Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Doris_Leuthard" title="Doris Leuthard">Doris Leuthard</a>, President <a href="/wiki/Johann_Schneider-Ammann" title="Johann Schneider-Ammann">Johann Schneider-Ammann</a>, Federal Councillor <a href="/wiki/Ueli_Maurer" title="Ueli Maurer">Ueli Maurer</a>, Federal Councillor <a href="/wiki/Simonetta_Sommaruga" title="Simonetta Sommaruga">Simonetta Sommaruga</a>, Federal Councillor <a href="/wiki/Guy_Parmelin" title="Guy Parmelin">Guy Parmelin</a> and Federal Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Corina_Casanova" title="Corina Casanova">Corina Casanova</a></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since 1999, an initiative can also be in the form of a general proposal to be elaborated by Parliament, but because it is considered less attractive for various reasons, this form of initiative has yet to find any use.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">That is a majority of 23 cantonal votes because the result of the popular vote in the six traditional <a href="/wiki/Half-canton" class="mw-redirect" title="Half-canton">half-cantons</a> each counts as half the vote of one of the other cantons.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-156">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2008, the ETH Zürich was ranked 15th in the field <i>Natural Sciences and Mathematics</i> by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Shanghai Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> and the EPFL in Lausanne was ranked 18th in the field <i>Engineering/Technology and Computer Sciences</i> by the same ranking.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Nobel prizes in <a href="/wiki/Non-science" title="Non-science">non-science</a> categories included.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>

         <li id="cite_note-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-47">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Swiss border ("Les principales rectifications postérieures à 1815 concernent la vallée des Dappes en 1862 (frontière Vaud-France, env. 7,5 km2), la valle di Lei en 1952 (Grisons-Italie, 0,45 km2), l'Ellhorn en 1955 (colline revendiquée par la Suisse pour des raisons militaires, Grisons-Liechtenstein) et l'enclave allemande du Verenahof dans le canton de Schaffhouse en 1967.")</i> in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hls-dhs-dss.ch/textes/d/D7841.php"><span title="Swiss border (">German</span></a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hls-dhs-dss.ch/textes/f/F7841.php"><span title="Swiss border (">French</span></a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hls-dhs-dss.ch/textes/i/I7841.php"><span title="Swiss border (">Italian</span></a> in the online <i><a href="/wiki/Historical_Dictionary_of_Switzerland" title="Historical Dictionary of Switzerland">Historical Dictionary of Switzerland</a></i>..            <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFRico_Kütscher2014" class="citation news cs1">Rico Kütscher (28 June 2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nzz.ch/wirtschaft/krankenkassen-koennen-ihre-effizienz-und-ihr-image-verbessern-1.18332345">"Kundenzufriedenheit: Krankenkassen sollten Effizienz und Image verbessern"</a>. <i>Neue Zürcher Zeitung, NZZ</i> (in German). Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 April</span> 2015</span>. <q>Wie es um die Kundenzufriedenheit in der Branche generell steht, zeigt eine 2013 im Auftrag von «K-Tipp» durchgeführte repräsentative Umfrage unter Versicherten, die in den vergangenen zwei Jahren Leistungen von ihrer Krankenkasse in Anspruch genommen haben. Beim Testsieger Concordia waren rund 73% der Versicherten «sehr zufrieden». Bei grossen Krankenkassen wie der CSS und Helsana betrug dieser Anteil 70% beziehungsweise 63%. Groupe Mutuel erreichte rund 50%, und die Billigkasse Assura kam auf 44%. Dies illustriert, dass die Zufriedenheit durchaus hoch ist – dass es aber auch Potenzial für Effizienzsteigerungen bei Krankenkassen gibt.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Neue+Z%C3%BCrcher+Zeitung%2C+NZZ&amp;rft.atitle=Kundenzufriedenheit%3A+Krankenkassen+sollten+Effizienz+und+Image+verbessern&amp;rft.date=2014-06-28&amp;rft.au=Rico+K%C3%BCtscher&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nzz.ch%2Fwirtschaft%2Fkrankenkassen-koennen-ihre-effizienz-und-ihr-image-verbessern-1.18332345&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASwitzerland" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>

                 <div>
                  <div class="plainlist">
                   <ul>
                    <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
                    <li><sup>2</sup> Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.</li>
                   </ul>
